## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / constitutive modeling (thermoelasticity and thermoplasticity)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly indicates a material constitutive law with thermo-mechanical coupling. Common relationships include elastic (Hookean), thermoelastic (thermal strain offsets), and temperature-dependent elasticity/yield/plastic hardening forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Hooke's law (1D): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain linear elasticity)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness softening/stiffening with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential-in-T): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (strong thermal sensitivity of stiffness over a range)
- Thermoelastic strain offset (with reference temperature): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion induces stress under constraint)
- Thermoelastic with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (combined modulus change and thermal strain)
- Nonlinear elasticity (polynomial): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (hyperelastic-like response in 1D approximation)
- Nonlinear elasticity (power law): sigma = c0 * Abs(epsilon)**c1 * sign(epsilon) (symmetric tension/compression nonlinear elastic scaling)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type compliance form: epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * Abs(sigma)**c2 * sign(sigma) (elastic + nonlinear strain; invertible to sigma(epsilon) in fitting)
- Bilinear elastoplastic (idealized, piecewise): sigma = Min(c0 * epsilon, c1 + c2 * (epsilon - c3)) (elastic region then linear hardening; c3 is yield strain)
- Voce-type hardening in strain (saturation): sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (flow stress saturates with plastic straining; often used as sigma(epsilon))
- Johnson–Cook-like multiplicative structure (reduced): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (work hardening times thermal softening factor, simplified)
- Eyring/thermal-activation-like flow (implicit, rearrangeable): sigma = c0 + c1 * asinh(c2 * epsilon) * (c3 + c4 * T) (rate/temperature-activated flow approximations expressed vs strain surrogate)
- Thermal softening via rational factor: sigma = (c0 * epsilon) / (c1 + T) (simple phenomenological reduction of stiffness/stress with temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion under constraint → use an additive strain shift: sigma depends on (epsilon - c*(T - c_ref)) rather than epsilon alone.
- Elastic modulus temperature sensitivity → put T inside a prefactor multiplying epsilon: sigma = E(T) * epsilon with E(T) as (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T).
- Material nonlinearity at larger strain → include higher powers of epsilon or |epsilon|^n with sign(epsilon) for symmetric tension/compression.
- Yielding behavior → piecewise or Min/Max structures capturing an initial linear branch transitioning to a weaker-slope hardening branch.
- Hardening saturation → use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) to model diminishing incremental stress with strain.
- Thermal softening of flow stress → multiply the strain-hardening term by a decreasing function of T (e.g., c0 + c1*T with negative c1, or 1/(c0+T)).
- Reference temperature effects → include (T - c_ref) rather than T to represent stress-free state at a particular temperature.
- Coupled nonlinear thermo-mechanics → allow cross terms like epsilon*T or epsilon*(T - c_ref) inside polynomials to capture interaction beyond pure prefactors.

GT’s defining structure includes the **product** \((T-T_0)\log(\epsilon+1)\) (i.e., a term linear in \(T\) whose coefficient is \(\log(\epsilon+1)\)). None of the candidates contains a term of the form \(T\cdot \log(\text{affine in }\epsilon)\) (or \((T-\text{const})\cdot \log(\epsilon+1)\)). Some candidates have \(\log(\epsilon+1)\) alone (30, 37), and many have logs of \(T\) alone, but no candidate can generate the required multiplicative coupling exactly by parameter choice or by a reasonable domain restriction (domain restrictions can handle Abs/Max/sign issues, not convert \(\log(Tc+1)\) into \(T\) identically on an interval, nor create a missing product term).

Therefore, no candidate can be made mathematically identical to GT on any plausible continuous domain by choosing constants.

## GT Analysis

The GT expression is:
```
96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*(T - 352.18) + 1) - 0.4785*(T - 352.18) + 8.062*(T - 352.18)*log(epsilon + 1)
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 0.00975*352.18 + 1)` = `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 3.4338 + 1)` = `96.829*epsilon*(-0.00975*T + 4.4338)`
  = `96.829*(-0.00975)*epsilon*T + 96.829*4.4338*epsilon`
  = `-0.9443*T*epsilon + 429.24*epsilon`

- Second term: `-0.4785*T + 0.4785*352.18` = `-0.4785*T + 168.52`

- Third term: `8.062*(T - 352.18)*log(epsilon + 1)` = `8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

So GT = `-0.9443*T*epsilon + 429.24*epsilon - 0.4785*T + 168.52 + 8.062*T*log(epsilon+1) - 2839.3*log(epsilon+1)`

The GT has these basis function terms (in T and epsilon):
1. `T*epsilon` (linear in both)
2. `epsilon` (linear)
3. `T` (linear)
4. constant
5. `T*log(epsilon+1)`
6. `log(epsilon+1)`

Now I need to check which candidates can reproduce these exact basis functions.

For candidates with `Abs(epsilon)`: since epsilon ≥ 0 (domain constraint), `Abs(epsilon) = epsilon`.

Key structural elements needed:
- `T*epsilon` term (from `T*epsilon^c` with c=1)
- `epsilon` term
- `T` term
- constant term
- `T*log(epsilon+1)` term
- `log(epsilon+1)` term

Let me check candidates systematically. Many candidates have the form `T*c0 + T*c1*|epsilon|^c2 + ...`. Setting c2=1 gives `T*epsilon`, which is one needed term. The `T*c0` gives the `T` term.

The critical question is whether the remaining terms can produce: `epsilon`, constant, `T*log(epsilon+1)`, and `log(epsilon+1)`.

### Candidates with `exp(c*sin(...))` terms (1, 3, 4, 6, 9, 10, 11, 18):
These contain `exp(c*sin(...))` which cannot produce `T*log(epsilon+1)` or `log(epsilon+1)`. These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**Candidates 1, 3, 4, 6, 9, 10, 11, 18: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidates with `sin(c*log(...))` terms (2, 14, 15, 16, 17, 19, 20):
`sin(c*log(c*|epsilon|+1) + c)` cannot equal `T*log(epsilon+1)` (no T dependence in the sin term, and sin ≠ log).

**Candidates 2, 14, 15, 16, 17, 19, 20: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidates with `exp(c*|epsilon|)*log(T*c + 1)` terms:
This is `log(T*c5 + 1)` NOT `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are different: one is log in T, the other is T times log in epsilon.

However, `log(T*c5 + 1)` ≈ `log(c5) + log(T + 1/c5)` which is NOT `T*log(...)`.

Wait - but can `exp(c4*epsilon)*log(T*c5+1)` somehow match `T*log(epsilon+1)`? No. `log(T*c5+1)` is logarithmic in T, while GT needs linear in T. And `exp(c4*epsilon)` is exponential in epsilon, while GT needs `log(epsilon+1)`.

These are fundamentally different basis functions.

**Candidates 21-50 (all with `exp(c*|epsilon|)*log(T*c+1)`): [NO MATCH]**

### Candidates 5, 7, 8, 12, 13, 35:
- **Candidate 5**: Has `T*c0*|epsilon|^c1 + T*c2*exp(c3*|epsilon|) + T + c4 + c5*sin(...)`. No `T*log(epsilon+1)` term. [NO MATCH]
